--- Commit Message ---
LU-7236 ptlrpc: idle connections can disconnect

 - when new request is being allocated ptlrpc initiates
   connection if it's not connected yet
 - if the import is idle (no locks, no active RPCs, no
   non-PING reply for last osc_idle_timeout seconds),
   then pinger tries to disconnect asynchronously
 - currently only client-to-OST connections can be idle
 - lctl set_param osc.*.idle_timeout=N controls new feature:
   N=0 - disable
   N>0 - seconds to idle before disconnect
 - lctl set_param osc.*.idle_connect=N to reconnect if idle
   (N is positive number)
 - OSC module parameter osc_idle_timeout controls default
   idle timeout and set to 20 seconds by default

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2017-07-17 09:46:23.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

hmm, but the server expects such a client to be alive and respond to pings, otherwise the client will be judged as a dead and the openhandle closed forcefully?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2017-07-17 18:08:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

Alex, I'm not sure what you mean.  My intent is that instead of saving open file handles as saved RPCs (after the RPC has committed on the server) that are resent during recovery, the RPCs sent are instead regenerated at recovery time from the open file handles.

This can reduce complexity in the ptlrpc layer, because we don't need to special-case saving open RPCs after they are committed, gets us closer to simplified interoperability, and may allow disconnected clients to keep open file handles if they don't have any locks.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2017-07-17 18:11:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

same here :) if the client is disconnected, then how MDT can maintain client's file open/pinned (e.g. protect from destroy) ?

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2017-10-05 08:01:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 43:

Conceptual question before I look at the patch:
What is the wait before disconnecting?
Presumably reconnection has a cost, so I think we don't want to disconnect *immediately* when idle.

Also, what if a large part of a system is idle for a long time (for example, a long running job not using Lustre), then suddenly goes active - We would then get a huge number of connections suddenly to the file system.  Is that OK?  I guess if we know it can happen...  But I am not sure our field people would like that surprise.

So, I guess - Could this be configureable, so we could disable it if it caused trouble?  Assuming it's not already.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2017-10-05 08:04:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 43:

Ah, I see we're only going to disconnect if there are *no* locks, which means we'd have to wait for at least the lru_age timeout, so that is (currently, I guess) our effective 'idle' timer.

Still feel this should be switchable somehow.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2017-10-05 12:45:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 43:

this functionality can be disabled with osc.idle_support=0 parameter.
probably this can be enough for the first approach?

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2017-10-05 12:48:00.000000000) ---
Patch Set 43:

I've heard many times that usually every client interacts with a subset of OSTs.
if this is correct, then no connection will be instantiated to OSTs a client doesn't need in the first place.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2017-10-05 12:50:42.000000000) ---
Patch Set 43:

as for time before disconnect the thing is driven by pinger which takes place if no activity  has been happening to a connection over obd_timeout
and you're right, the patch doesn't disconnect if it's referenced (by locks, for example).

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2017-10-05 14:39:49.000000000) ---
Patch Set 43:

Yes, that sounds good.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2017-10-28 03:37:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 49:

(9 comments)

Looks fairly straight forward.  Do you have any tests that actually verify this?  One option would be to make "idle_disconnect_sec" hold the time before disconnect, and then set it very low for a test?  I'd think that this may otherwise cause the clients to disconnect right at mount time if they don't have any locks.

At one time when we did purely on-demand connections after mount, several sites didn't like this because it gave the false impression that the filesystem was working properly, when in fact some OST is totally offline and the client didn't know since it never tried to connect.

In that light, clients should at least try to connect to all targets initially, even if they will disconnect after some shorter interval if they haven't been used.
